  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer3879360185911261434">It happens at the start of every November: the Scorpio Races. Riders attempt to keep hold of their water horses long enough to make it to the finish line. Some riders live. Others die.<br/><br/>At age nineteen, Sean Kendrick is the returning champion.   <span id="freeText3879360185911261434" style="display:none">It happens at the start of every November: the Scorpio Races. Riders attempt to keep hold of their water horses long enough to make it to the finish line. Some riders live. Others die.<br /><br />At age nineteen, Sean Kendrick is the returning champion. He is a young man of few words, and if he has any fears, he keeps them buried deep, where no one else can see them.<br /><br />Puck Connolly is different. She never meant to ride in the Scorpio Races. But fate hasn’t given her much of a chance. So she enters the competition — the first girl ever to do so. She is in no way prepared for what is going to happen.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/350572-is-this-as-terrible-as-shiver-or-has-the">Is this as terrible as Shiver or has the author actually learnt to write?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_350572'><a id="like_count_community_question_350572" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/350572?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">14 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F10626594-the-scorpio-races">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/350572-is-this-as-terrible-as-shiver-or-has-the">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/350572-is-this-as-terrible-as-shiver-or-has-the">See all 6 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/40013263-carly"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/40013263-carly">Carly</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Shiver was agonizing. I could not get through the trilogy, and I could not bear to read one more line about how much the characters were infatuated wi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Shiver was agonizing. I could not get through the trilogy, and I could not bear to read one more line about how much the characters were infatuated with each other, entirely dependent on the love of the other. The Scorpio Races is my favorite book, and it was nothing like the Shiver trilogy. Stiefvater was able to compose a plot independent of a love story, and the romance that she did include was appropriately limited. I personally felt connected to all of the characters in the book as well as the setting, which certainly did not happen in Shiver.<br /><br />That being said, this is not a piece of literature that will be remembered throughout time. Her writing is simplistic because it is aimed at younger readers. Everything is stated, not much left to interpretation. Her language is beautiful, but it cannot compare to that of the classics. If you are looking for good writing, this is it. If you are looking for great writing, search elsewhere. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2156674833" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2156674833" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2156674833?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-rivals-to-lovers">trope-rivals-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-sff">ya-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-slow-burn">trope-slow-burn</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2156674833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15535876571053389608">“<em>It is the first day of November and so, today, someone will die</em>.”<br/><br/>With these haunting words laid out like a feast of uncertainty and doom, Maggie Stiefvater launches a new telling of an old tale inspired by elements of Celtic mythology, legends of the water horses, and her own imagination.<br/><br/>And nothing had ever been more beautiful, or fearsome, or bizarre.<br/><br/><u>
  <strong>So, what's this book about?</strong>
</u><br/><br/>Each October, dread settles over the island of Thisby, as The Scorpio sea throws <em>capaill uisce</em>—commonly known as </span>
  <span id="freeText15535876571053389608" style="display:none">“<em>It is the first day of November and so, today, someone will die</em>.”<br /><br />With these haunting words laid out like a feast of uncertainty and doom, Maggie Stiefvater launches a new telling of an old tale inspired by elements of Celtic mythology, legends of the water horses, and her own imagination.<br /><br />And nothing had ever been more beautiful, or fearsome, or bizarre.<br /><br /><u>
  <strong>So, what's this book about?</strong>
</u><br /><br />Each October, dread settles over the island of Thisby, as The Scorpio sea throws <em>capaill uisce</em>—commonly known as water horses—onto its shore, and a hint of fear mingles with the ocean breeze as the dreamlike unreality of such delectable creatures warries with the gruesome truth of their deadly nature. Every first of November—a date bound to loom large in the landscape of the islanders’ mind—the Scorpio Races are held, and young men compete in a beachfront race to the death astride the <em>capaill uisce, </em>with such longing in them, all bound up in hesitancy, as though they yearned for connection, but the mounts didn’t reciprocate their desires.<br /><br />Sean Kendrick has carved his life out of the land of sea and sand and fatal, beautiful horses. Four-years running champion of The Scorpio Races, he is locally reputed as the best<em> capaill uisce</em> trainer, but he remains bound to the wealthy Malverns for whom he works as a stable hand. Of all the things Sean Kendrick has conjured in years of yearning for an independent life, buying the right to his water-horse stallion, <em>Corr</em>, was a thing he only folded inside his heart, until he was assailed anew by the brew of feelings that had churned in him at the terrible clear-eyed certainty that it was <em>now or never</em>.<br /><br />Katherine “Puck” Donnelly becomes the first woman to ever compete in the Scorpio Races, rolling the dice on her own survival for her family’s sake, which had seemed—after her eldest brother decided to move to the mainland and abandon her alongside her younger brother—to be drifting away from each other like untethered boats in the mercy of the tides. Signing up with her simple land mare, Puck knows that her chances are slim but she was so far down this path that to turn around would be to face a howling, dark tunnel with nothing at its end. And with that realization, Puck feels it take root within her, this <em>purpose</em>, as though speaking it gave it the light it needed to grow.<br /><br />Puck is a counterpoint to Sean, both of them forged the horrific day they’ve been orphaned by the <em>capaill uisce</em>, both of them saddled with the determination to win the race, both of them creatures riddled with empty spaces that swelled and hurt with the same species of hope: fragile and sullied by fear and uncertainty. <strong>But there could be only one winner.</strong> So is it  possible that all their jagged edges might fit together like puzzle pieces, or would they look to each other for the faith they kept between them, and begin to find only doom instead?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“I say, 'I will not be your weakness, Sean Kendrick.'<br />Now he looks at me. He says, very softly, 'It’s late for that, Puck.'”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />While the world that Stiefvater builds here is thinly sketched, formed only roughly with a few shadows here and there, like wisps of smoke, it's <em>tantalizing</em> rather than incomplete, and it’s more than enough to leave the vibrant suggestion of magic. <em>The Scorpio Races</em>, ultimately, is a set of brilliant moments woven together with a sure hand, and structured around a simple plot that illuminates, with rich prose and richer structure, a set of very real, very damaged, very hopeful characters learning the courage it takes to reveal their authentic selves to each other and to the world.<br /><br />This is the kind of story that circles around you two, three times before drawing you in to an oddly poetic tale of magic and passion, desire and longing. It’s so easy to let your mind relax into the fantasy of it, and let the familiarity of Stiefvater's storytelling and characterization wear away all the sharp, startling edges of a novel world, and an even more unfamiliar myth. <br /><br />I loved every minute of it.<br /><br /><strong>I also love Sean and Puck so much</strong> I wish I could put them in a giant envelope and mail them away from all the bad guys.<br /><br />From the beginning, they feel like characters you’ve known for years. It’s not that they’re tropes—far from it—but Stiefvater is just so deft at crafting characters that feel fully fleshed-out and more real than reflections in a mirror. There was so much in them, a lifetime’s worth of feeling and yearning—many lifetimes’ worth—concentrated into a single moment at the end, and it made reading this book feel like being locked out of a room while someone you love is trapped inside with unknowable terrors. I love how Puck fought with impressive assertiveness everyone who belittled her for imagining she could possibly have had the bad taste to compete in a sport “designated for men”, and how Sean fought for his right to claim Corr with every scrap of will and had none left over for meekness.<br /><br />But as much as I love them individually, collectively they just…<em>set ablaze</em> the entire story. There is so much else going on in their lives—hellish, heavenly and in-between—but together, they have a way of being untouchable, of being above, peering down at the rest of the islanders from some lofty place they made from their ragged hearts and every moment of peace they stole from the jaws of chaos. I love how they were both rooting out darkness in each other: desire and faith they’d never imagined themselves capable of, and how the stone foundation of their romance was a deep love found in companionship and mutual respect. It wasn’t something they eagerly sought, it just came to them naturally, when it was time, and it was just so [clutches chest] so <em>beautiful</em>.<br /><br />I don't how else to say “<strong>I love this book so much”</strong> and make you eager to read it, but I'll say this: if I could just steal a moment from this story—the breeze scented with the last dying gasp of winter and tracing across closed eyelids, the ground soft and sandy, the ocean rocking against the shore, the freedom and these moments of being “<em>so, so alive”</em> on a horse’s back ripping through the wind—and exist in it forever, I would be so content.<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="15535876571053389608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer380843125" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18045346437258706878"><b>[read 4 | sept 2020]</b><br/>I missed this book so much 😭 I actually teared up while listening to the audio again, and I sit here in awe of the craft and skill that went into making a book feel so ancient and beautiful, reckless and solid, wild and aching. It's phenomenal, one of the best books I've ever read. I just want to fold into the pages never leave.<br/><br/><br/><b>[read 3 | november 2017]</b><br/>So I purely reread this for the aesthetic of NOVEMBER 1st. Go me. I am shallow and great. <b>And also I love this book so bloody </b></span>
  <span id="freeText18045346437258706878" style="display:none"><b>[read 4 | sept 2020]</b><br />I missed this book so much 😭 I actually teared up while listening to the audio again, and I sit here in awe of the craft and skill that went into making a book feel so ancient and beautiful, reckless and solid, wild and aching. It's phenomenal, one of the best books I've ever read. I just want to fold into the pages never leave.<br /><br /><br /><b>[read 3 | november 2017]</b><br />So I purely reread this for the aesthetic of NOVEMBER 1st. Go me. I am shallow and great. <b>And also I love this book so bloody much it actually hurts my heart.</b> I am hopelessly and utterly in love with Sean and Corr and Thisby and every word choice is so PERFECT that it melts me.<br /><br /><b>Notable Thoughts:</b><br />• can Holly pls adopt Sean<br />• Puck keeps trying to be less vinegar but she should be all the vinegar<br />• 99% sure Finn has OCD and it is such a good rep<br />• Gabe and Tommy Falks are my new ship don't @ me<br />• SEAN FREAKING KENDRICK &lt;3 &lt;3<br />• also shout out to the fact that this is truly the best romance of life and Sean and Puck like barely have to hold hands or kiss to be the most beautiful relationship of the world<br />• also why can't I have more<br />• sean tho<br />• i need to go sit down i have emotions<br /><br /><br /><b>[read 2 | june 2016]</b><br /> This book means <i>so very much to me</i>. You know those books that are just <i>yours</i> for some reason? This one = mine. It started me on YA. I read it after The Hunger Games and there was noooo going back afterwards. YA OBSESSION HERE WE COME. Not to mention my deep eternally wildly fangirling permanent adoration of <i>all things</i> Stiefvater. She is my most favourite author of the universe. Why? THIS IS WHY. Flawless books of utter writing perfection and characters that steal your heart. omg. <b>I honestly...I'm just a mess of feelings</b>.<br /><br />Re-reading this was like coming home to old friends. It's been 4 years since I read it. I FORGOT SO MUCH. I had like 9 anxieties reading it <i>even though I'd already read it</i>. I <b>fell hopelessly back in love with Sean Kendrick.</b> It's the quietness. I LOVE QUIETNESS. Sean says 1 word where everyone says 6. Me toooooo. Or else I say 0 words where everyone says 6 and wait until they're definitely listening to talk. His non-talking-ness just resonated wtih me. aGAIN. And <b>Puck's vinegar and sugar temperament I just love endlessly.</b> ALSO <b>FINN</b>; the precious. He is probably one of the bestly written characters with <b>OCD I've ever read</b>...especially in a fantasy!! (I think Maggie Stiefvater has OCD, right? So you can tell this is just crafted so beautifully and thoughtfully.) (I just wish I knew how old he was, dangit. I just KEEP WONDERING. I'm going to say 13 maybe?)<br /><br />The way Thisby always catches my heart so much.<br /><br /><b>Needless to say: this is one of my all time favourite books of the universe.</b><br /><br />(Note:the audiobook is freaking fantastic by the way. BEST choice for the re-read. The actors are impeccable and it has music by Maggie Stiefvater.)</span>

<div id="review_2548090898" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2548090898" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2548090898?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407129853" href="/book/show/11210739-the-scorpio-races">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2548090898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7504870111899708376"><i>”Somewhere close by, a man is moaning; he’s been trampled or thrown or bitten. He sounds resentful or surprised. Did no one tell him that pain lives in this sand, dug in and watered with our blood?”</i><br/><br/>I really don’t know where I should start with this review because just like any of Maggie’s other books this one wasn’t only magical but also so damn atmospheric that it’s more than just hard to put my feelings into proper words. There is something in the way she writes that always captures the emotio</span>
  <span id="freeText7504870111899708376" style="display:none"><i>”Somewhere close by, a man is moaning; he’s been trampled or thrown or bitten. He sounds resentful or surprised. Did no one tell him that pain lives in this sand, dug in and watered with our blood?”</i><br /><br />I really don’t know where I should start with this review because just like any of Maggie’s other books this one wasn’t only magical but also so damn atmospheric that it’s more than just hard to put my feelings into proper words. There is something in the way she writes that always captures the emotions and the essence of a certain season or time. In <b>“Shiver”</b> it was winter, in TRC it’s that foggy, otherworldly atmosphere of Cabeswater and in <b>“The Scorpio Races”</b> it was autumn and the daily life on an island. <br /><br />I swear I could <u>
  <b>feel</b>
</u> the cold autumn wind on my skin and I could <u>
  <b>smell</b>
</u> the leaves and the sea with my nose while I read this book. It was done so perfectly that I immerged into a totally different world and just like Puck and Sean (and Craig ;-P) I couldn’t help but fall in love with the capaill uisce. Those water horses were so awesome, I can’t even! &lt;333<br /><br /><i>”The capaill uisce plunged down the sand, skirmishing and bucking, shaking the sea foam out of their manes and the Atlantic from their hooves. They screamed back to the others still in the water, high wails that raised the hair on my arms. They were swift and deadly, savage and beautiful. The horses were giants, at once the ocean and the island, and that was when I loved them.”</i> <br /><br />I love how Maggie described them and I also love that she researched the myths and folklore of water horses. They are indeed very fascinating and if you want to delve a little deeper you just have to look them up under <b>“cabyll-ushtey”</b>. Anyway, back to the actual water horses of this book! They were amazing and I loved their beautiful, violent and graceful nature! It’s kind of obvious Maggie has some experience with horses because I think otherwise she would have never been able to write about them so convincingly. There’s a deep respect in her words and you can feel it whenever you read Sean’s or Pucks POV! And tell you what? I loved that aspect of the book! It made it so good and realistic that I was almost convinced those horses actually exist. *lol* <br /><br />And this ultimately brings me right to the two main characters of <b>“The Scorpio Races”</b>. Puck Connolly and Sean Kendrick! &lt;333<br /><br /><i>”And then I see him. A dark-haired boy who is made of all corners. He is standing next in line by the counter, silent and still in his blue-black jacket, his arms folded across his chest. He looks out of place and wild in here: expression sharp, collar turned up against the back of his neck, hair still windblown from the beach.”</i><br /><br /><i>”My mother always said that I was born out of a bottle of vinegar instead of born from a womb and that she and my father bathed me in sugar for three days to wash it off. I try to behave, but I always go back to the vinegar.”</i> <br /><br />I adored them both! XD Sean Kendrick was a mystery to everyone but himself and Puck Connolly was an open book that had its own secrets. They were two really intriguing characters and before I even knew it, I was already pulling for them. *lol* Even though they both had a rather rough life they still decided to fight for their dreams and they truly did everything possible in order to achieve their goals. They really dealt with every blow that came their way and they did it with fierce determination! &lt;3<br /><br /><i>”The truth is this: for eleven months of the year I make myself valuable to Malvern, and then for one month, I make myself invaluable. Would he be willing to give up that one month to keep the other eleven? Am I willing to risk it?”</i><br /><br /><i>”Why is it that going away is the standard? Does anyone ask you why you stay, Sean Kendrick?”<br />“They do.”<br />“And why do you?”<br />“The sky and the sand and the sea and Corr.”</i><br /><br />This is such a perfect quote because Sean and Puck <b>ARE</b> the embodiment of the island. They are deeply rooted in its sand and unlike so many of the islands other inhabitants they can’t even imagine to leave it one day. It’s their heart, their home and the place they belong to and I think Maggie conveyed that feeling more than just well. =) Still, the island is its own entity and there are people that make it hard to enjoy the wilderness of this land. First and foremost Benjamin Malvern and his demon of a son called Mutt. <br /><br /><i>”And I told you before, I’ll sell you any of the thoroughbreds.”<br />“I didn’t make any of those thoroughbreds. I didn’t make them what they are.”<br />Malvern says, “You made all of them what they are.”<br />I don’t look at him. “None of them made me who I am.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Mr Kendrick was born on a horse and he’ll die on one, and maybe that’s not something you can breed for. He’s one of those rare men who can make a horse work for him but never asks for more than they have.”</i><br /><br />It was so obvious that Benjamin Malvern had a deep respect for Sean, yet at the same time he refused to let him go. Ever the business man he tied him to his stable making him just another one of his precious horses. I hated Benjamin Malvern so much for that and I despised him even more for being aware of Sean’s talent and keeping him under his thumb. And I don’t even want to speak about Mutt Malvern that – excuse my crude language – sadistic douche bag! Gosh, there were moments I wanted to slap some sense into him and I am a pacifist and actually never slapped anyone. (My only weapons are words! *lol*) <b>ARGH!</b> Just to think about Mutt makes my blood boil, such a despicable a******!!! &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><i>”At the sound of them, the red stallion flinches, as if the bells are physically painful, and I find myself unexpectedly blinking away tears. <br />Sean Kendrick turns his face away.<br />There’s something so wretched in that that I can’t just leave him there by himself.”</i><br /><br />I swear Sean and Puck had to put up with so many things before the races and I loved them so much for never giving up! Plus I also liked that Puck was the first woman to ever take part in the races! Thank you Maggie for inventing a strong female character people are able to look up to! We still need more of those! &lt;3 And last but not least another thing I’m very thankful for: A slow, realistic burn and a relationship that was built on mutual respect and the love for their horses and home!!! <b>THANK YOU SO MUCH FOR THAT!!!</b> &lt;333<br /><br /><i>I say, “I will not be your weakness, Sean Kendrick.”<br />Now he looks at me. He says, very softly, “It’s late for that, Puck.”</i><br /><br />All told I really loved this book! <b>“The Scorpio Races”</b> was an awesome “ride” and the ending was as bittersweet as dark chocolate with a pinch of salt in it. T_T<br />Highly recommended and definitely once again an amazing Maggie Stiefvater book! ;-)<br /><br />Since this was another buddy read with my amazing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/86429475-craig" rel="nofollow noopener">Sugar Bun</a> I want to use the chance to thank him for this cool and funny BR! I think our next one is already pending. Do you still have a copy of <b>“Linger”</b>? *lol* I have the feeling that you’ll need a yucky romance soon. Haha! ;-P</span>
  <a data-text-id="7504870111899708376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_178767097" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178767097" />
    <a title="Lyndsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey"><img alt="Lyndsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288890060p2/4224396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178767097?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyndsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyndsey" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey">Lyndsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=pov-alternating">pov-alternating</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=reviewed-2-stars">reviewed-2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=1st-person">1st-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=about-animals">about-animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=blog-giveaway-at-strangemore">blog-giveaway-at-strangemore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=about-horses">about-horses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=made-me-yawn">made-me-yawn</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178767097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9537556301516216775"><b>Also posted on <a href='http://www.STRANGEMORE.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>STRANGEMORE.COM</a>.</b><br/><br/>This is basically the paranormal version of Misty of Chincatigue with (gasp!) romance!<br/><br/>Like Hidalgo, on the beach instead of the desert with (gasp!) kissing! Between two riders! NOT between the horse and it's rider though. Well... sometimes between the horse and it's rider. Just a little.<br/><br/>When this book started, it felt like a breath of fresh sea air, not rife with the smell of YA cliche. That was mainly because I <b>thought</b> this book was told from the alternating persp</span>
  <span id="freeText9537556301516216775" style="display:none"><b>Also posted on <a href="http://www.STRANGEMORE.com" rel="nofollow noopener">STRANGEMORE.COM</a>.</b><br><br>This is basically the paranormal version of Misty of Chincatigue with (gasp!) romance!<br><br>Like Hidalgo, on the beach instead of the desert with (gasp!) kissing! Between two riders! NOT between the horse and it's rider though. Well... sometimes between the horse and it's rider. Just a little.<br><br>When this book started, it felt like a breath of fresh sea air, not rife with the smell of YA cliche. That was mainly because I <b>thought</b> this book was told from the alternating perspective of two <i>boys</i>, Sean and Puck, which would have been a nice change for Steifvater. Maybe I was in the mood for a buddy story or a brother story, instead of the usual stereotypical romance. But it wasn't meant to be, you see, because Puck is a SHE and not a he. (Sorry, my inner Dr Suess came out for a second.)<br><br>Not that this is a spoiler or anything, as it it mentioned fairly quickly. It was just something my mind was set against. I wanted Puck to be a boy. I'm tired of the "here's a girl who does this and here's a boy who does that, hmmmm, I wonder when and how they'll meet and, gee, wouldn't it be weird if they fell in love, because, oh boy, we've never seen THAT happen before."<br><br><b>
  <u>The Rundown</u>
</b><br><br>I understand now why the blurb is so impossibly vague. This is a difficult book to sum up.<br><br>Two individuals, Sean and Puck, are preparing separately for the annual Scorpio Races (where the dangerous water horses of Thisby face off against each other with their riders and generally lots of bloodshed) until their lives eventually collide into each other. Sean is the typical Thisby teen boy who just so happens to compete every year in the races. Puck is a young girl having some family issues, in particular with her brother's desire to leave the family home and the island that they live on, and she thinks that competing in the Races will force her brother to stick around. But Puck decides to race her regular horse against the blood-thirsty water horses, which cause quite a stir and tons of problems. And that's just the beginning.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Writing and World-Building</u>
</b><br><br>If there was one word to describe this book, it would definitely be "atmospheric." The descriptions <i>were</i> gorgeous, but the location for the book is more than a little mind boggling. It seems to be a created fantasy island located in Ireland? I think. The term they use for the water horses is a Gaelic term but it takes place on a fictional island, I guess? The specifics are never really laid out about where or what or when this "Thisby" is.<br><br>Many reviewers raised concerns about the lack of world-building in the Maggie's Wolves of Mercy Falls series. That being said, I feel like she almost went in the opposite direction with way too much world-building, including tiny details about minor characters, and it honestly wasn't very interesting to me. The characters all had their own quirks and backgrounds, but we were told too much and too often about them. More than was necessary.<br><br>However, the world that she built around The Scorpio Races was much better than the world of Mercy Falls. The prose isn't quite as purple and the romance isn't nearly as cheddar. I'd say it's more like a magenta colby jack. It was just a very bland and tasteless magenta colby jack.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Pacing</u>
</b><br><br>Pacing was my biggest problem with The Scorpio Races. It takes at least 100 pages or so before anything remotely interesting happens. Usually by then, I would have put a book down not knowing whether or not I would pick it back up, but because this is an upcoming release, I felt like I needed to keep going. In addition, because of the way the environments are described and the action builds slowly, a certain intrigue simmers in your mind and drives you forward regardless of the slow start. But I'm not entirely sure that the pay-off was worth the anticipation.<br><br>Around page 380, the seemingly fabled races begin. Now that would have been a great place to start the book! Because up until that point almost NOTHING had happened. It was all setup. I'm sorry, but I do not <i>need</i> three hundred and eighty pages of <u>setup</u>. Even if it has pretty words and HORSES!!!<br><br>Because by the time that part finally came around and I thought, "Now this could be interesting," -- it was much too late. I was looooong past mentally checked out and had become disinvested and disinterested.<br><br><u>This might come off rude, but this is the best way I know how too explain what it seems like has happened.</u><br><br>You know when a little girl first discovers the way her skirt twirls when she spins? It's cute, right?! You're like, "Oh, isn't that precious. She's twirling." But then it's <u>two weeks later</u> and she's STILL twirling like the world won't be able to turn itself if she stops, you're like "Okay, we get it! You can <i>twirl</i>" But you can't say that because then you're just being an asshole for ruining a little girl's "twirl time."<br><br>Well, Maggie Steifvater can twirl... and whirl... and swirl... and canter... and whinny. It just seems like the author discovered for the first time "Wow, I can write pretty prose. Let's throw some more of that in there."<br><br>Don't get me wrong: It <i>is</i> pretty. But holy well of words, do we need SO much of it?<br><br>The Scorpio Races don't actually happen until the last 20 or 30 pages of the book, and even then, the actual Races only last about 12 pages, the rest is aftermath. For a book that's 410 pages long, that is not a good chunk of the content. Only about 3 percent of it, in fact. Maybe it should have been titled "The 380 pages leading up to the Scorpio races".<br><br>I mean, sure, Hunger Games had some setup as well. But it would have been an entirely different book had the Games only lasted 12 pages.<br><br><b>
  <u>Who Should or Should Not Read It</u>
</b><br><br>I wouldn't read this book again. And I wouldn't recommend it for a lot of people. But I think a lot of people will read it anyway.<br><br>Here's why:<br>1) It is written by Maggie Stiefvater.<br>2) It is a paranormal written by Maggie Stiefvater.<br>3) It is a paranormal written by Maggie Stiefvater about HORSES! HORSES! HORSES! HORSES! HORSES! HORSES!<br>254) It is a standalone. (Finally!)<br><br>If you hated Shiver, then you'll probably hate this one as well. If you loved Shiver, then you might love this one.<br><br>Right around the time that the Black Beauty movie with Chris O'Donnell came out, I went through horse phase like many young girls probably do. But I got over it and I think I'm still over it, which might be why I didn't love this book. I also went through a dog phase, Old Yeller, Rin Tin Tin, Turner and Hooch, except that I never grew out of it and never will.<br><br>I think Horse People will love this book. Keep in mind that there is a big difference between <i>liking</i> horses and being a Horse Person. I <i>like</i> horses. They are pretty and I like to imagine them with horns or wings or gills, but my thoughts don't revolve around them. I am a Dog Person.<br><br>I've heard people say that horses are like really big dogs, but I think that those people are just Horse People trying to convince you to be a Horse Person. When really, it's like comparing Chihuahuas to Labradors. Some people say that small dogs and big dogs are the same. They aren't. Not even close. Usually, those who say that are Small Dog People trying to convince you to be a Small Dog Person. This isn't to say that any of them are better or worse than the other, they are just <i>different</i>. I am a Big Dog person, not a Horse Person, not a Small Dog Person.<br><br>If this had been about magical sea-faring German Shepherds, I would have LOVED it.... probably.<br><br><u>
  <b>Other Thoughts</b>
</u><br><br>The one thing I really like about what Maggie did with this book, though the same may not be said for Shiver, is that she didn't follow the <i>pack</i> with The Scorpio Races. After the vampire-werewolf craze hit and SMeyer announced on her website that she was writing a mermaid book, strangely, we saw a surge in the number of mermaid based books on the market, many of a questionable quality due to the fact that they were most likely rushed onto the shelves. Maggie didn't go with the surge but she didn't go against it either. She went along side it by creating her own mythology similar to many ocean based tales. It wouldn't be surprising if we see a rise in ocean based mythology books after The Scorpio Races.<br><br>Although the pacing is slower and the story not quite as involving as Shiver, this book still seems to be a step in a better direction (albeit almost too far a step) for Maggie. The world-building is much more fully realized and detailed than that of Shiver and the storyline isn't purely romance based, which leads me to think that maybe, just <i>maybe</i>, authors <b>do</b> pay attention to reviewers complaints. Maybe she just decided to put more time into her world-building on her own, or maybe, hopefully, we are having some <i>minuscule effect</i> on how the book world evolves. And that makes me very VERY happy.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Verdict</u>
</b><br><br>The Wolves of Mercy Falls was just a little too soft for me and the Scorpio Races was just a little too hard, so maybe by the time the next book comes around from Ms Stiefavter, that one will be <i>juuuuust right</i> for this little goldilocks.<br><br>I'm giving it two stars because it was written well, just badly paced and plotted, in my opinion. The pretty words weren't enough to make up for the boredom. And unfortunately, I never connected to the characters or the romance between them.<br><br>The thing that frustrates me the most about books is when feel like I didn't learn anything. I don't really mind not being entertained if I take something away from it that I had never thought about before. But I at least want one or the other.<br><br>If you aren't going to entertain me, then teach me something. If you aren't going to teach me something, then by George Washington, at least ENTERTAIN me!! I'm very sorry to say that this book did neither. But that isn't to say that you will feel the same.<br><br>Personally, I didn't love it. I don't think I even liked it, but it wasn't terribly written; it wasn't too terribly involving either.<br><br>Meh. That's my word for this book. Or rather more like -<br><br><i>MEEEEEEEEEEEEEEAAAAAAAH.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380351949i/705506.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah, I just whinnied. Whatcha gonna do about it, huh?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9537556301516216775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11722786414008578780">this book was not what i was expecting. not in the least. i went into this thinking it would simply be an action-packed tale of a daring race; but what i got was so, so much more. <br/><br/>i found myself comforted by a story that showed, in a very special way, that sometimes life is not about what you want, but what you need. with lush and poetic prose (which is so on brand for stiefvater), this story weaves together a foundation of desire, love, and strength in a way that tugs at your heartstrings. <br/><br/>wow.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14784597087244390369"><b><a href='https://www.amazon.com/Scorpio-Races-Maggie-Stiefvater-ebook/dp/B0051WIX24/ref=sr_1_4?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1506126938&sr=1-4' rel='nofollow noopener'>GET IT HERE</a> FOR $1.99! 9/22/2017!</b><br/><br/><i>"This Skarmouth is raw and hungry, striving and unknowable. Everything the race makes me feel on the inside is bleeding up through the seams in the street tonight."</i> - Sean Kendrick <br/><br/><i>"I wonder how long it will take for me to feel as adult on the inside as I look on the outside."</i> - Puck Connolly<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473311617ra/20444652.gif' width='500' height='222' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>*deep breath*</b><br/><br/>Sometimes you read a book and it becomes your whole world while you are reading it. For me, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races' title='The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Scorpio Races</a> is one of those books. <br/><br/>I am just <u>forever in debt</u> to</span>
  <span id="freeText14784597087244390369" style="display:none"><b><a href="https://www.amazon.com/Scorpio-Races-Maggie-Stiefvater-ebook/dp/B0051WIX24/ref=sr_1_4?s=digital-text&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1506126938&amp;sr=1-4" rel="nofollow noopener">GET IT HERE</a> FOR $1.99! 9/22/2017!</b><br><br><i>"This Skarmouth is raw and hungry, striving and unknowable. Everything the race makes me feel on the inside is bleeding up through the seams in the street tonight."</i> - Sean Kendrick <br><br><i>"I wonder how long it will take for me to feel as adult on the inside as I look on the outside."</i> - Puck Connolly<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473311617ra/20444652.gif" width="500" height="222" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>*deep breath*</b><br><br>Sometimes you read a book and it becomes your whole world while you are reading it. For me, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races" title="The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scorpio Races</a> is one of those books. <br><br>I am just <u>forever in debt</u> to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater" title="Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Maggie Stiefvater</a> because this book has truly affected me. <b>It's very difficult for me to put into words.</b><br><br>But I suppose the best way I can say it is this: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races" title="The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scorpio Races</a> is the kind of story I would hope to write, if I had the talent.<br><br>It's <u>incredibly unique.</u> Stiefvater's writing is totally immersive. So much detail, and yet all of it felt relevant. I savored every word, every page, every single bit of this book that I could. <br><br>I have heard some say that it was too slow, and I understand that critcism. It just wasn't true for me and my personal reading experience. <b>
  <u>Yes it was slow, but I feel that it absolutely needed to be.</u>
</b><br><br>This is a story that blooms in its own time, a breathtaking experience if given the proper patience.<br><br>While I read this, I was on the island of Thisby. I could feel the cold November breeze threading through my hair, I could smell the tinges of brine and blood on the waves that soaked the shoreline. I could hear my heart beating in my ears as the events unfolded. <i>And I read the last thirty pages of this story with tears streaming down my face.</i><br><br><b>I'm just so damn emotional, and sitting here in a heap of my feelings.</b><br><br>I know this review isn't very specific, but it suffices to say that I loved <i>everything</i>. From the characterization, to the world building, to the plot, to the writing style - it's the whole package. I couldn't recommend this book enough, especially for fans of Stiefvater's other works.<br><br>Now please excuse me while I go recover in a dark corner somewhere.<br><br><i>This and other reviews of mine can be found on <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/34-mary-s-reviews/422-thescorpioraces" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Nest</a>!</i></span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5365999-caz-littlebookowl?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5365999-caz-littlebookowl?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284576824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9517483136453975044">3.5/5 stars!<br/><br/>I really liked The Scorpio Races, and I'm glad I listened to it on audiobook. Since there were two voice actors it was very easy to separate Puck and Sean, which was lucky since I've heard that some readers found it very difficult to distinguish between them when reading the book. The narrators also had very different ways of speaking as the characters, which made it impossible to mix the two up while listening.<br/><br/>The writing was beautiful. There is such a rich atmosphere, and the descr</span>
  <span id="freeText9517483136453975044" style="display:none">3.5/5 stars!<br /><br />I really liked The Scorpio Races, and I'm glad I listened to it on audiobook. Since there were two voice actors it was very easy to separate Puck and Sean, which was lucky since I've heard that some readers found it very difficult to distinguish between them when reading the book. The narrators also had very different ways of speaking as the characters, which made it impossible to mix the two up while listening.<br /><br />The writing was beautiful. There is such a rich atmosphere, and the descriptions left vivid images of the setting in my mind. I felt like I was there on Thisby, experiencing the world alongside Puck and Sean. Whilst the setting was strong <i>on</i> Thisby, I didn't get a strong sense of <i>where</i> Thisby was located on the map. I'm assuming it's a fictional island, but there was a reference to the States, so there is some blend with our present world.<br /><br />My main concern was the slower pace, though I think my expectations hindered my full enjoyment of the story. I went into this expecting a lot of action, but instead found my thoughts wandering a lot, but when my attention returned I didn't feel like I missed much. <br /><br />I was also hoping for a little more explanation about the history of the Scorpio Races and how the tradition came to be. With a slower pace, there is plenty of room to explore the origins of Thisby's traditions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9517483136453975044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1243717174" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1243717174?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243717174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11145917811178698493"><i>"It's easy to convince men to love you. All you have to do is be a mountain they have to climb or a poem they don't understand."</i><br/><br/>Puck has a horse, two brothers and soon no house to call a home. Sean's heart beats for something that he doesn't own. Both have no choice and only one chance to get what they desperately need. It's either win or die.<br/><br/>Why did I not pick this up sooner?<br/>This totally deserves the 5 star rating. My heart goes out to every single tiny detail of this book. But most of all for </span>
  <span id="freeText11145917811178698493" style="display:none"><i>"It's easy to convince men to love you. All you have to do is be a mountain they have to climb or a poem they don't understand."</i><br /><br />Puck has a horse, two brothers and soon no house to call a home. Sean's heart beats for something that he doesn't own. Both have no choice and only one chance to get what they desperately need. It's either win or die.<br /><br />Why did I not pick this up sooner?<br />This totally deserves the 5 star rating. My heart goes out to every single tiny detail of this book. But most of all for the oh so precious characters. I'm a little in love with all of them, but very much so with Finn.<br /><br />I'm at loss with words and it's too late to form a clear thought, especially now that <i>The Raven King</i> is waiting for me to be read. A+ for world building, plot, characters, writing, unpredictability and magic. Perfect from start to finish.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_229068650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229068650" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229068650?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407129853" href="/book/show/11210739-the-scorpio-races">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=multiple-povs">multiple-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=amazing-writing">amazing-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=my-flat-army">my-flat-army</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=role-models">role-models</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2011">reviewed-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=books-i-can-t-wait-to-read-in-2011">books-i-can-t-wait-to-read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229068650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8590608683345519408"><b>They came in with the tide. The moon illuminated long lines of froth as the waves gathered and gathered and gathered offshore, and when they finally broke on the sand, the <i>capaill uisce</i> tumbled onto the shore with them. The horses pulled their heads up with effort, trying to break free from the salt water.</b><br/><br/>I had to restrain the squealing, fangirly Maja and shove her in the closet so that the adult, critical Maja can sit and write this review. Believe me, it’s better this way. <br/><br/>With The Scorpio Rac</span>
  <span id="freeText8590608683345519408" style="display:none"><b>They came in with the tide. The moon illuminated long lines of froth as the waves gathered and gathered and gathered offshore, and when they finally broke on the sand, the <i>capaill uisce</i> tumbled onto the shore with them. The horses pulled their heads up with effort, trying to break free from the salt water.</b><br><br>I had to restrain the squealing, fangirly Maja and shove her in the closet so that the adult, critical Maja can sit and write this review. Believe me, it’s better this way. <br><br>With The Scorpio Races, Maggie Stiefvater has finally earned my complete trust. I promise never to doubt her again. I’ve read four of her books so far and I gave all four of them five stars. If there was ever an author who deserved my wholehearted support, it’s her. She is an artist above all else, and if that alone isn’t enough, here’s another reason for my respect:<br><br><i>Other writers might have different priorities, but for me, the chief goal of my novels is not plot or premise or pacing, but to evoke a certain feeling. <b>I will sacrifice most anything in order to change someone's mood in a certain way.</b> I can't do that without careful navigation of metaphor and character development.</i><br>(From <a>Ms. Stiefvater’s blog post</a>)<br><br>But I’ll limit my praise to The Scorpio Races for now:<br><br>This time, Stiefvater flirted a little more seriously with the fantasy genre and created an amazingly gripping story.<br>People on the fictional island Thisby live and breathe for one thing and one thing alone: wild and bloodthirsty water horses, the <i>capaill uisce</i>. They are either directly involved in the races or they take care of tourists from the mainland. Even though the Scorpio Races are held only once a year, the heartbreak and the loss they inevitably bring are almost too big for one small island. People die in the races. They die because they are too slow, too vulnerable or too ready to trust the monsters they are riding on. The <i>capaill uisce</i> may be stunningly beautiful, but all you have to do is turn your back on them for one short second, and their teeth will already be deep inside your flesh. <br><i>It takes everything in me not to whimper. The creature is black as peat at midnight, and its lips are pulled back into a fearsome grin. The ears are long and wickedly pointed toward each other, less like a horse and more like a demon. They remind me of shark egg pouches. The nostrils are long and thin to keep the sea out. Eyes black and slick: a fish’s eyes.<br>It still stinks like the ocean. Like low tide and things caught on rock. It’s barely a horse.<br>It’s hungry.</i><br><br>Kate “Puck” Connoly and her two brothers lost their parents when a bloodthirsty <i>capall uisce</i> attacked them on the sea. Ever since, the three of them survive by fixing things for other people, making teapots, helping in the local store and doing anything at all to put some butter and flour in their mostly empty pantry. But when the oldest brother, Gabe, the only one with a steady job, decides to leave the island, and Benjamin Malvern threatens to take their house away, Puck sees no other choice but to join the dangerous race in order to save her house, and maybe even prevent her brother from leaving. <br><br>Sean Kendrick lost his mother to the mainland and his father in the race. Enormous talent and love for the <i>capaill uisce</i> made it possible for him to survive on the island, working for Benjamin Malvern and his obnoxious son Mutt. Sean has won the races four out of six times. He has everyone’s respect and a decent amount of money saved. The only thing stopping him from leaving the Malverns is Corr, the <i>capall uisce</i> that is Sean’s only family. This year more than ever Sean has to win the races because if he wins, Benjamin Malvern will finally sell him Corr, thus setting them both free. <br><br>Make no mistake: even though this story is told from two alternating POVs and it seemingly focuses on Sean and Puck, it’s really a story about the water horses. They are what matters, Sean and Puck are just tour guides. If you’re looking for romance, you could end up disappointed. It is present, but the emphasis is on other things this time. The writing is atmospheric and it feels like a thick mist, albeit one you're in no hurry to get out of. The island itself is a character: people, mentality and everyday struggles they face. The rich American buyer, George Holly, is there to remind us exactly how different the island people are. <br><br>Please follow the link above to find out more about Stiefvater's writing priorities. She is one amazing lady and she just keeps proving her worth over and over again with every new word she writes.<br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_165654013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165654013" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165654013?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=huge-disappointments">huge-disappointments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=paranormal-general">paranormal-general</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=too-many-povs">too-many-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=mythic-and-fairy-tale-ish">mythic-and-fairy-tale-ish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=supportive">supportive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165654013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6965136437216878859">Killer water horses + Maggie Stiefvater. What could go wrong?<br/><br/>As it turns out, quite a lot. I feel just terrible writing this, and if you want to know just how much, it actually took me 4 months to make myself finish the book--partly because I wasn't engaged in the story, but also because I could sense that this wasn't going to be good reading experience. After the bruising my heart took with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9409458.Forever__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___3_' title='Forever (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #3) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Forever</a>, I really didn't want to write a second negative review for this author. But I'm afraid my disapp</span>
  <span id="freeText6965136437216878859" style="display:none">Killer water horses + Maggie Stiefvater. What could go wrong?<br /><br />As it turns out, quite a lot. I feel just terrible writing this, and if you want to know just how much, it actually took me 4 months to make myself finish the book--partly because I wasn't engaged in the story, but also because I could sense that this wasn't going to be good reading experience. After the bruising my heart took with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9409458.Forever__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___3_" title="Forever (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #3) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Forever</a>, I really didn't want to write a second negative review for this author. But I'm afraid my disappointment continues.<br /><br />The story centers around violent, flesh-eating water horses called <i>capall uisce</i> who are used in a race on the beach on the fictional island of Thisby every November. From clues dropped throughout the book, it seems that the events take place sometime during the 20th century, though not in present day, and the choice to be vague about the location and time work well for the backdrop of the story, particularly in setting up the hardscrabble life, antiquated attitudes, and the pressing need for money. Puck Connolly is hoping to win enough money to keep her parents' house. Sean Kendrick wants to win his fifth race so he can buy the horse he's come to love. The entire island is focused on the race, both out of fear of the unpredictable water horses and out of desire for the material gains it may bring.<br /><br />I love the concept of this story, and some of the writing is very evocative. Unfortunately, the framework and plotting feel very loose to me, as characters wander in and out of scene to have meaningful conversations with one another, to posture and bluff, and to strain for glimpses of people or horses throughout much of the story, all without a whole lot of substantial action to back them up. It takes a loooong time to set up Puck's entering the race with an ordinary mare, and a looooong time for the two main characters to meet. While I'm not a fan of characters who swoon all over each other as soon as they meet, I'm also not a fan of reading hundreds of pages in which not very much happens at all. Well, there are a number of violent deaths of both human and horse randomly inserted into the story, but few of them were particularly affecting to me, as there was so little time setting them up or dealing with the aftermath that none of them felt particularly real.<br /><br />Aside from lack of action, however, I also had a number of issues with the writing. I think too many authors use alternating perspectives these days, and it becomes a problem when the second POV adds little to the narrative and when the two voices sound so very similar. I had to flip back several times to figure out who was actually speaking, since they're both mucking around with horses and entering races and butting up against one obstacle or another. Add to this an unfortunate tendency to repeatedly use both first and last name when referring to a character we've known forever (as late as on the second to last page), chapters that are often too short, chapters that too often end on heavily meaningful statements, an incredibly annoying insertion of a name that sticks out like a sore thumb, and it all becomes a pretty frustrating reading experience. My biggest issue, though, is that so much of this just did not resonate emotionally with me. There are plenty of justifications on paper for why Puck stubbornly defies tradition and why there is sabotage and so on and so forth, but...I just didn't believe in it all enough to care. And being that I was willing to believe in water horses that kill people for no reason whatsoever, that's really saying something.<br /><br />All in all, there wasn't enough here to keep my interest, though I know that many of my fellow Stiefvater fans have enjoyed it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6068551.Shiver__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___1_" title="Shiver (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Shiver</a> is still one of my favorite books of all time, but I've yet to read another book by this author that comes close to living up to it. Will I keep looking for a Maggie book that thrills me and moves me to the same degree? Sure I will. But with 380 pages of build-up, 12 pages of the actual race race, and 12 pages of wrap-up, <i>The Scorpio Races</i> certainly isn't it.<br /><br />**Coming back later to edit this review and to insert more specific examples and quotes, but I wanted to get my thoughts down before I let the review drag out for as long as my reading experience did!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6965136437216878859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1264904127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10718696596096564904"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459199608i/18581450._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>► <b>I reckon the reasons for which <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races' title='The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Scorpio Races</a> weaved itself throughout my beloved favorites could cause an opposite reaction to other readers</b>. Do I care, though? No, because every slow-paced page, every heartfelt and beautiful sentence, every haunting and atmospheric landscape, every <i>inch</i> of Sean's bloody-stained jacket and killer horse reminds me that if nothing else, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races' title='The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Scorpio Races</a> has a <i>soul</i>, and <b>I'm consumed by it</b>.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"I am here on firm ground, but part of me is already down on the be</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10718696596096564904" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459199608i/18581450._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► <b>I reckon the reasons for which <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races" title="The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scorpio Races</a> weaved itself throughout my beloved favorites could cause an opposite reaction to other readers</b>. Do I care, though? No, because every slow-paced page, every heartfelt and beautiful sentence, every haunting and atmospheric landscape, every <i>inch</i> of Sean's bloody-stained jacket and killer horse reminds me that if nothing else, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races" title="The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scorpio Races</a> has a <i>soul</i>, and <b>I'm consumed by it</b>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I am here on firm ground, but part of me is already down on the beach, and my own blood is singing <i>I'm so, so alive</i>"</b>
</blockquote><br><i>Sigh</i>. I've been trying to put my thoughts into words for hours now, but it seems that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races" title="The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scorpio Races</a> joined the very exclusive club of the novels which mute my abilities to express myself. Puck and Sean's story is burned into my brain, though, twisting my perception of the reality around me, Thisby's landscapes forever ingrained in me. That's why I cannot, I will not leave this space blank and no matter how impossible it seems at this time, I'll try to do this wonderful book justice. Sorry in advance if I don't succeed. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Outside, the wind is a live, starving thing. The sky over Skarmouth is a dull brown, lit by the streetlights, but everywhere else is inky."</b>
</blockquote><br>■ If you're - even a little - accustomed to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater" title="Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Maggie Stiefvater</a>'s books, it shouldn't come as a surprise that <b>the writing is nothing short of spectacular</b> : compelling and beautiful, warming your heart a second and breaking it the next. How could I complain about the slow-pacing if I thought it was <i>
  <b>perfect</b>
</i> for the story? I'll tell you, I can't. Is it subjective? Sure it is, and I understand the readers who were bored out of their minds. Yet I wasn't. Never at any moment. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Why aren't you going?"<br>The question infuriates me. I demand, "Why is it that going away is the standard? Does anyone ask you why <i>you</i> stay, Sean Kendrick?"<br>"They do."<br>"And why do you?"<br>"The sky and the sand and the sea and Corr."</b>
</blockquote><br> ■ I genuinely think that your ability to enjoy - to love - the plot depends on your expectations. <b>Does <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races" title="The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scorpio Races</a> revolve around the sea killer horses and the race taking place every year on Thisby's beach? Sure, but if you think that's all it is about, you will be disappointed</b>. Many readers pointed it, and they're right : the race doesn't start until the very end, and is only an excuse to deal with the real issues in my opinion. <br><br>What issues? <br><br>The raw and frightening feelings one can experience when not sure if he - she - <b>belongs somewhere</b>. Through Sean, Puck, Gabe, Finn's eyes, we witness different ways to answer the difficult question of who they really are and what they need to do to find happiness. Is it staying, whatever it takes? Is it leaving? Is compromising themselves <i>okay</i> to reach their goals? As much as I personally find that the "coming-of-age" label is often misleading, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races" title="The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scorpio Races</a> it rises to a whole new level. I couldn't be indifferent to their struggles, because as strange as it might be (given the fantasy elements) <b>they felt real and heartbreaking and oh so moving</b>. Beware of the harshness, though : many parts are - really - difficult to handle, especially because <b>it contains cruelty toward animals</b>. <br><br>■ As usual <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater" title="Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Maggie Stiefvater</a> nailed her characterization</b>. If I sure didn't agree with every decision they took, none of her characters felt wasted and all of them provoked contradictory feelings in me. Honestly, they're just so freaking amazing : <u>well rounded-up, fleshed-out, and a little heartbreaking</u>. <b>Sean, in particular, made it impossible for me to <i>not</i> love him almost instantly</b> : his wildness, his loyalty to Corr, his sea horse, his intensity - <b>that boy didn't need to talk for me to be lost forever</b>. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"All I know is that Sean Kendrick rode that bay mare and waited until he was nearly over the cliff edge before saving himself, and that the dead speak more than he does."</b>
</blockquote><br>► <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races" title="The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scorpio Races</a> changed me, somehow, even if I can't pinpoint in what way so far, and this story will linger for a very long time in my heart. Now, tell me, what better compliment could I give it? <b>None</b>.<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="10718696596096564904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
