<div id="review_1891179601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1891179601" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1891179601?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545224918" href="/book/show/15827344-the-scorpio-races">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=this-shit-made-me-cry">this-shit-made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=author-love">author-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=catharsis-dot-mp3">catharsis-dot-mp3</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1891179601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12253134648534049834"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>It feels like he's confessed that he's dying of a disease I've never heard of, with symptoms I can't see. The utter wrongness of it, the way it won't fit in my head, keeps coming back to me again and again, as if I've only just learned about it. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>The Scorpio Races</i> is about man-eating horses, but it's more about <b>finding where you belong</b>. Here, two very different people try to hold onto the things they love most, even as their world spins around them. <br/><br/>Maggie Stiefvater's writing style i</span>
  <span id="freeText12253134648534049834" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>It feels like he's confessed that he's dying of a disease I've never heard of, with symptoms I can't see. The utter wrongness of it, the way it won't fit in my head, keeps coming back to me again and again, as if I've only just learned about it. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><i>The Scorpio Races</i> is about man-eating horses, but it's more about <b>finding where you belong</b>. Here, two very different people try to hold onto the things they love most, even as their world spins around them. <br /><br />Maggie Stiefvater's writing style is just as gorgeous as ever. She manages to fit so many emotions into such short paragraphs without having to tell anything. It's all shown. <br /><br />As is usual with her books, I only realized how invested I was in these characters when the book hit the conclusion. These two leads were both <b>well-crafted characters.</b> Puck is strong and sassy and utterly believable. The relationship between Sean and his horse, Corr, especially slayed me. Even side characters like Finn are instantly believable with strong voices. <br /><br />There's also a great romance between the two leads. <b>No instalove</b> to be found here– they go from reluctant friends to allies to something more. They fit together like puzzle pieces, and I love that– how they make each other better. <br /><blockquote>
  <i> I think every now and then about Sean's thumb pressed against my wrist and daydream about him touching me again. But mostly I think about the way he looks at me — with respect — and I think that's probably worth more than anything.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I've only recently begun to realize the importance of setting in books, and The Scorpio Races definitely benefits from setting. The island is at once rugged and wild and claustrophobic and terrifying and beautiful. These characters love the island so much that even in moments of fear and terror, the island is lovely. I had such a vivid picture of the island in my head by the end. <br /><br />Essentially my only complaint is that this book takes too long to get going. Yes, I love slow-build plots as much as the next person, and the slow-build plot works to its best here. But I still spent around half the book wanting things to <i>just get going.</i> Adjust your expectations— this story is a <b>slow build to a brilliant conclusion,</b> not a fast-paced ride. <br /><br />The ending makes every moment worth it, though. <b>The last chapter genuinely made me cry.</b> What an emotional, perfectly-written section. That section alone gets five stars from me. <br /><br />This is a completely different story than the Raven Cycle, but it worked for the same reasons the Raven cycle worked, so I would definitely recommend this to anyone who enjoyed that book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12253134648534049834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1782969187" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15637823425239780575"><br/>Buddy reading this with <s> my queen, <i> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1662750539?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Em</a> (rip) </i></s>  my girl, <i> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1753819266?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Empress</a> </i> <s> but they both have no chill so I'm going ahead and starting. :) </s><br/><br/><br/><b> Maggie Stiefvater has built a world that I want to live in forever. </b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481855387i/21461932._SY540_.jpg' width='380' height='620' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i> The Scorpio Races </i> is a slightly mystical, slightly historic, all-around awesome tale narrated by our two main characters, Sean Kendrick and “Puck” Kate Connolly. Every November the Scorpio Races take place which is a race where riders must hold their water horses away from the siren waters long en</span>
  <span id="freeText15637823425239780575" style="display:none"><br>Buddy reading this with <s> my queen, <i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1662750539?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Em</a> (rip) </i></s>  my girl, <i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1753819266?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Empress</a> </i> <s> but they both have no chill so I'm going ahead and starting. :) </s><br><br><br><b> Maggie Stiefvater has built a world that I want to live in forever. </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481855387i/21461932._SY540_.jpg" width="380" height="620" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> The Scorpio Races </i> is a slightly mystical, slightly historic, all-around awesome tale narrated by our two main characters, Sean Kendrick and “Puck” Kate Connolly. Every November the Scorpio Races take place which is a race where riders must hold their water horses away from the siren waters long enough to cross the finish line. Sounds simple, but it’s not. Many die and there is only one winter. <br><br>Sean Kendrick, (who is literally my everything) is a four-time winning champion at nineteen-years old. Sean is a mysterious, solemn young man who is known, but no one <i> knows. </i> Puck Connolly, on the other hand, finds herself in a situation where she <i> has </i> to ride in the dangerous races. So much is riding on both of their shoulders as the preparation for the races begins. <br><br><i> “Not a jockey?” Holly says to me as I walk Miracle back into the yard. <br>“Just a horse lover,” I reply. </i> <br><br>Never have I read a book so built and raw and real. Maggie has an incredible talent when it comes to writing. The world of Thisby that she slowly crafted is not just words on a paper but images and ideas and tastes and smells. <br><br>The characters, like everything else about the book, are not stereotypical, they are not obvious or obnoxious or common. They are hand-crafted and so so so <i> real. </i> <br><br>Also, Sean Kendrick is everything. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481855387i/21461933._SX540_.jpg" width="430" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The thing about Maggie’s books are that they are slow. They are slow like a burning flame that melts away the unknown to reveal the plot, the story, the characters, the romance, the friendships, the conflict, and the conclusion. <br><br>This book has burnt a special place in my heart. <br><br>Also, Finn. Finn Connolly is so damn precious. Someone please give him lots of machines and gears and all the November Cakes in the world. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481855387i/21461934._SY540_.jpg" width="380" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><i> “There are moments that you'll remember for the rest of your life and there are moments that you <b> think </b> you'll remember for the rest of your life, and it's not often they turn out to be the same moment.” </i><br><br><br><br>5 stars!!<br></span>

<div id="review_2153628205" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2153628205" />
    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2153628205?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407129853" href="/book/show/11210739-the-scorpio-races">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2153628205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1591050406843639136"><i> "The water horses are hungry and wicked, vicious and beautiful, hating us and loving us. It is time for the Scorpio races." </i><br/><br/>I really enjoyed venturing into one of Maggie's earlier books. I loved The Raven Cycle, and although this book is very different from that series, I found it just as fun.<br/><br/>Puck Connelly has lived on Thisby her entire live, she knows the way things are - the harshness of the landscape, and sometimes also the harshness of its inhabitants. When her oldest brother Gabe announces</span>
  <span id="freeText1591050406843639136" style="display:none"><i> "The water horses are hungry and wicked, vicious and beautiful, hating us and loving us. It is time for the Scorpio races." </i><br /><br />I really enjoyed venturing into one of Maggie's earlier books. I loved The Raven Cycle, and although this book is very different from that series, I found it just as fun.<br /><br />Puck Connelly has lived on Thisby her entire live, she knows the way things are - the harshness of the landscape, and sometimes also the harshness of its inhabitants. When her oldest brother Gabe announces that he is leaving the island, Puck enters into The Scorpio Races, both to keep her brother around longer, and also with the slim chance of winning the prize money. She however, has chosen to ride on her own horse, a land horse rather than the traditional choice of mount, and she would also be the first female rider to ever compete.<br /><br />The Scorpio Races are usually only on water horses, ones that people catch from the sea and attempt to train and ride. But their nature cannot be altered, and there are often many tragedies and deaths from these <i>capall uisce</i>.<br /><br />The second POV aside from Puck's is Sean Kendrick. Another islander whose father was killed in The Scorpio races when he was a young boy, but this doesn't stop Sean from entering the competition each year and winning the past 4 years in a row.<br /><br />I loved both characters, how they stood out and you really got to know them. I also really appreciated the slow burn romance - I definitely shipped it!<br /><br /><i> "I think every now and then about Sean's thumb pressed against my wrist and daydream about him touching me again. But mostly I think about the way he looks at me - with respect - and I think that's probably worth more than anything." </i><br /><br />At times pretty gruesome, but this was a story unlike any I've read before and I thoroughly enjoyed it. <br /><br /><i> "Because...if you feed the island blood before the race, maybe she won't take as much during it." </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1591050406843639136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_235809778" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235809778" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235809778?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">horse-fans, fans of complex YA</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=lovely-lovely-language">lovely-lovely-language</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy-ya">urban-fantasy-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library-kindle">my-library-kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235809778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16945865494241534489"><br/>Tarot card reading for this book: inverted Tower. The Tower is leaning into the sea, crumbling, with thrashing waves and stormy skies, and while it can be a card of destruction, it can also be a card of fundamental change--which describes The Scorpio Races down to the letter.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363205i/714479._SY540_.jpg' width='200' height='240' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>A fierce and hungry book. Even the wind is hungry here, <b>"a live, starving thing." </b>The tomboyish Kate, otherwise known as 'Puck,' and her brothers have been orphaned ever since the carnivorous water horses killed their paren</span>
  <span id="freeText16945865494241534489" style="display:none"><br>Tarot card reading for this book: inverted Tower. The Tower is leaning into the sea, crumbling, with thrashing waves and stormy skies, and while it can be a card of destruction, it can also be a card of fundamental change--which describes The Scorpio Races down to the letter.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363205i/714479._SY540_.jpg" width="200" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>A fierce and hungry book. Even the wind is hungry here, <b>"a live, starving thing." </b>The tomboyish Kate, otherwise known as 'Puck,' and her brothers have been orphaned ever since the carnivorous water horses killed their parents. Loss runs through Kate's thoughts daily, ghosts of her parents and the struggle of being a family when none of the remaining children is an effective adult. One night, her oldest brother announces his decision to emigrate to the mainland, motivating Kate to enter the annual horse race that celebrates the water horses' return to land. Even as the whole island survives because of the horses and the tourists they bring, there is a deep strand of ambivalence at the prospect of their return, as they inevitably bring carnage and death.<br><br>Narrative switches between Kate and Sean, both entrants into the lethal race. Sean is a little older, more independent, more sure, but half wild himself. He too has lost a parent to the horses, and the other to the mainland, but unlike Puck, he is only respectful of them, not fearful. A multiple race-winner, he has numerous little magics that assist him in control over the water horses--twine, spit, iron. When Puck meets him, she finds he is <b>"a dark-haired boy who is made of all corners."</b> Sean's storyline involves a jealous and vengeful beta-male attempting to best him with capturing and training the horses, not one of my favorite plots. Beta's actions perhaps goes over the top for the justification we are given.<br><br>I appreciated the extent to which the two voices are distinct in telling their stories. It's fascinating when they meet some of the same people, each describing and interacting with them in their own style. Puck is clearly younger, both developmentally and emotionally, but she's trying hard to grow up: <b>"I hope he doesn't, because my character's improved a lot since then. Nowadays I would've only <i>thought </i> the spitting part instead of saying it to his face." </b><br><br>One of the highlights of The Scorpio Races is the language. Deceptively simple language is used extremely well, creating atmosphere and character that stands out without cumbersome description. Even something as simple as Sean watching a man carving meat is described carefully: <b>"I am mesmerized by the utter unawareness of the entire process, the childlike pleasure Beech takes in a job ill done."</b> There's quite a few ugly occurrences in this book, but something about the prose makes it darkly beautiful: <b>"Padgett is beginning to look improbable; something about him is starting to look less like a man and more like meat."</b><br><br>I enjoyed the uniqueness of the mystical element in the water horses and the mythology of the island. The mythology behind their return plays second fiddle, however, as the focus for Puck and Sean is on survival, and the options for emotional survival that winning will bring. I love the visual of the horses riding the crest of a wave onto the sand, but their bloodthirstiness and destruction thread through the book in a dark weave. Still, Stiefvater captures their swift beauty, <b>"she is down the beach like an osprey diving for a fish"</b> and creates sympathy for Sean's longing and love for his own water horse, Corr. Puck's faithful pony, ("<i>horse!</i>") Dove stands in sharp contrast to the barely bridled wildness of the water horses, and her willing and realistically drawn great heart is one of the soft pleasures of the story. <b>"She is my mare and my best friend, and I keep waiting for some thing bad to happen to her, because I love her too much."</b><br><br>Overall, and enjoyable read that I'd recommend. It's grim but not despairing; there's a gently developed love interest that rises beyond the constraints of most YA romances, and the main characters are unique, sincere people doing what they can.<br><br><br>Cross posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/03/26/the-scorpio-races-by-maggie-stiefvater-or-water-horse-love/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/0...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16945865494241534489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1753390231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1753390231" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1753390231?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kaylin by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1753390231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13433386776599010328"><b> 3 Stars<br/><br/>Overview:</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“There are moments that you'll remember for the rest of your life and there are moments that you <b>think</b> you'll remember for the rest of your life, and it's not often they turn out to be the same moment.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Look, no one is more upset about this rating than me. I wanted to love this <i>so much.</i> I recently finished The Raven Cycle, and it became one of my favorite series. I’d heard so many great things about this, I was <i>sure</i> I’d love it.<br/><br/>...But I just feel really underwhelmed?<br/><br/><b>Pros:</b><br/><br/>I s</span>
  <span id="freeText13433386776599010328" style="display:none"><b> 3 Stars<br /><br />Overview:</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“There are moments that you'll remember for the rest of your life and there are moments that you <b>think</b> you'll remember for the rest of your life, and it's not often they turn out to be the same moment.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Look, no one is more upset about this rating than me. I wanted to love this <i>so much.</i> I recently finished The Raven Cycle, and it became one of my favorite series. I’d heard so many great things about this, I was <i>sure</i> I’d love it.<br /><br />...But I just feel really underwhelmed?<br /><br /><b>Pros:</b><br /><br />I still love Stiefvater’s writing style. There’s something incredible about the way she sets a scene, and this is one of the most atmospheric novels I’ve ever read. <br /><br />She also does a fantastic job of establishing character. A few chapters in you <i>feel</i> for these characters. You understand their struggles without being overwhelmed with information. <br /><br />These established characters are involved in some very real-feeling emotional conflicts and familial dynamics. Especially Puck’s relationship with her brothers. Their arguments were some of the strongest portions of the book, as no one was simply ‘wrong.’ <br /><br />I also really loved George Holly for some reason? His conversations with Sean were very interesting and further illustrated the strange atmosphere of this island. <br /><br /><b>Cons:</b><br /><br />I just never <i>connected.</i> <br /><br />I understood the characters and what they were struggling for, and in the first few chapters I really felt for them and was <i>certain</i> this book was going to make me cry. But by the end I was just questioning the logistics?<br /><br />Maybe it’s because I’m not a horse person. Maybe because I’m not familiar with the original mythology. Maybe it’s just me. <br /><br />But this was <i>odd</i> and I really struggled with suspending my disbelief. Which is strange, because I’m certain I’ve read weirder… but I kept stumbling over details?<br /><br />If Puck’s been raised on this island and loves it with all her soul, why does she know so little about the race proceedings? If everyone is so terrified of the horses, why do they race at all? I’m sure there is a larger theme about nationalism and man’s innate desire to prove one’s self… but so many people were dying? Why did no one rethink this dangerous game?<br /><br />Seriously everyone was fine with riding horses that <i>eat</i> people, but they couldn’t understand a woman participating in a ‘man’s’ race?<br /><br />The bad-guy also seemed a little stereotypical to me? Perhaps I didn’t connect with him enough either, but he just seemed fueled by a blind desire to win. <br /><br />90% of the book is a build-up for the race. This is okay with me, a I love slow paced stories that gradually build… but the pay-out didn’t seem worth it? The actual race lasted like 8 pages, and somehow ended up feeling rushed?<br /><br /><b>In Conclusion:</b><br /><br />It’s times like this I wonder if I read the same book as everyone else. The writing was there, but I just feel like I was missing <i>something</i> with the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13433386776599010328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <i>“I didn't know," I start truthfully, "that it was the hard way when I started on it.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I’ve h</span>
  <span id="freeText17047043483564783786" style="display:none"><b>Kindle Daily deal for <a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B0051WIX24/ref=x_gr_w_glide?caller=Goodreads&amp;callerLink=https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races&amp;tag=x_gr_w_glide-20" rel="nofollow noopener">$1.99</a> 10Sept17</b><br /><br />Buddy Read starting Feb 15, 2015 with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3250652-brandi" rel="nofollow noopener">Brandi</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7214073-nicholas" rel="nofollow noopener">Nicholas</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11494588-tandie" rel="nofollow noopener">Tandie</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5556618-sophie" rel="nofollow noopener">Sophie</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/210123-d-g" rel="nofollow noopener">D G</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4159427-athena-shardbearer" rel="nofollow noopener">Athena Shardbearer</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9274536-kerry" rel="nofollow noopener">Kerry</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17575003-mich" rel="nofollow noopener">Mich</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/2374349-ashleyr" rel="nofollow noopener">AshleyR</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10336538-jessica-rabid-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Jessica</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9026138-michelle-book-hangovers" rel="nofollow noopener">Michelle</a> at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a><br /><br /><br />Steve West has one of the sexiest voices ever. What a great time I had listening to this story all over again. Thanks buddy readers for a really fun reread of a story I enjoy. <br /><br /><b>Original Review:</b><br /><br />4.5 Stars<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“I didn't know," I start truthfully, "that it was the hard way when I started on it.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I’ve have never given a recommendation to specifically read or listen to book but I think for this one I will. I have found that the writing style of Maggie Stiefvater, it is slower and eloquent, lends itself better to being spoken aloud than reading. I don’t think I would have liked this book nearly as much had I read it. I feel the same way about Raven Boys also by Maggie and anything written by Lani Taylor. The audio version of the book has two different voices to relay the alternating POV of Kate (Puck) and Sean. Both narrators did an exceptional job with the cadence of the story and delivery of emotion. One of the best audiobooks I’ve listened to. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“My mother always said that I was born out of a bottle of vinegar instead of born from a womb and that she and my father bathed me in sugar for three days to wash it off. I try to behave, but I always go back to the vinegar.”</i>
</b><br /><br />This is not your typical YA book where there is always a lot of action happening and a faster pace. It takes some time for the story to get moving but I immediately liked the characters. Both are underdogs in their own way. Puck has lost both her parents and needs to win the purse for her family. Sean needs to win to be able to buy the waterhorse he loves and freedom for them both. Both have a set of obstacles to overcome and it could have worked out that they would end up enemies as competitors but remarkably they become friends.<br /><br /><i>“Where will you and Corr be?” I ask. <br />Sean presses two fingers along the edge of the counter, sweeping crumbs into a pile. I notice that his fingers are permanently dirt-stained like mine. He says, “Right next to you and Dove.” <br />I stare at him. “You can’t risk not winning. Not because of me.” <br />Sean doesn’t lift his eyes from the counter. “We make our move when you make yours. You on the inside, me on the outside. Corr can come from the middle of the pack; he’s done it before. It’s one side you won’t have to worry about.”<br /><b>I say, “I will not be your weakness, Sean Kendrick.” <br />Now he looks at me. He says, very softly, “It’s late for that, Puck.”</b></i><br /><br />The race is fraught with danger, even the training is dangerous. The Capll uisce (waterhorses) are fierce and not to be trusted. There are some heart stopping events happening throughout the book but for the most part it is about the two people trying to get by with what they have been given and falling unexpectedly in love along the way. The romance however is very far from the front of the story. It is more about the Island, which is a character all of its own, as well as the sea and the Capall uisce. I was fascinated by the descriptions of this harsh Island world and the ferocious love that both Puck and Sean feel for somewhere that has taken so much from both of them. <br /><br />The actual race isn’t until the very end of the book and doesn’t take long. Much like an actually horse race a lot of banter before and then it is over in the blink of an eye. I really didn’t want it to end, I wanted to see if Holly came back in a year and his predictions were true. I wanted to stay with Puck and Sean and Finn even after the ending. The very ending was unexpected and beautiful, I teared up a little as I thought that it was a great example of love and sacrifice.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2073659803" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2073659803" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2073659803?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2073659803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13164405247347158557"><b>*** 4.75 ***<br/><br/>A Buddy Read with the MacHalo Freaks, because mythical blood-thirsty Water Horses are awesome!!!</b><br/><br/>Let me start by saying that very few authors are capable of affecting me emotionally the way Maggie Stiefvater does. Her prose is magic! I am not just spouting words here. Her writing hits somewhere in the vicinity of my soul and I can't get away unscathed. She wounds with her beautiful prose, enchants with her lyrical cadence of melody made of letters, and heals with the hope for salvatio</span>
  <span id="freeText13164405247347158557" style="display:none"><b>*** 4.75 ***<br /><br />A Buddy Read with the MacHalo Freaks, because mythical blood-thirsty Water Horses are awesome!!!</b><br /><br />Let me start by saying that very few authors are capable of affecting me emotionally the way Maggie Stiefvater does. Her prose is magic! I am not just spouting words here. Her writing hits somewhere in the vicinity of my soul and I can't get away unscathed. She wounds with her beautiful prose, enchants with her lyrical cadence of melody made of letters, and heals with the hope for salvation, as unlikely as it might seem… I have never been able to pick up a book of hers and put it down without feeling as if my mind is straddling both worlds - the real one and the one Maggie weaves us in. That is not to say that her work is perfect. It isn't and I am kind of glad for it, since it makes her more human and having read some of her interviews, if she reaches that panicle of perfection, she might decide she is over with writing and go on to music or any of the other talents G-d has gifted her with… I am glad to say, she has to keep on trying by giving us more and more of her enchanting stories…<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"…"“Tell me what to wish for." Tell me what to ask the sea for."<br />"To be happy. Happiness."<br />"I don't think such a thing is had on Thisby. And if it is, I don't know how you would keep it."…"</i>
</b><br /><br />The Scorpio Races is not what the book is really about. They are just the event the author has chosen in order to show us the lives of the people on the Island of Thisby, a harsh and economically depressed place, with little hope for the locals, with the youth finding their way either away to the main land, or often killed by the creatures that make the Island unique among any others… The <b>capaill uisce</b>, the mythical Water Horses which come to the beach every November and ride, taking down people as well as animals for their kills, and going back to the sea. Some know those as Kelpies and know how these horses born of mythology can be awe inspiring as well as blood-curdling terrifying. They are natural predators and their allure is what keeps the brave, sea-loving souls living on the Island, brings the tourists in November, which is the core of the local economy, and culls those who underestimate their viciousness, leaving behind widows, widowers, and many orphans. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"…"The water is still high and brown and murky with the memory of the storm, so if there’s something below it, I won’t know it. But that’s part of this, the not knowing. The surrender to the possibilities beneath the surface. It wasn’t the ocean that killed my father, in the end."…"</i>
</b><br /><br />Puck and her brothers are just this type of orphans. She is only 17, but their parents were killed by the water horses years ago, leaving her, her older brother Gabe and her younger brother Finn to fend for themselves. The only thing she possess is her mare Dove and she cares for her as best as she can. Puck loves the island and wants to find a way to keep her life there. However, her older brother has been deeply disillusioned and is headed out, away from everything this Island represents for him, to the Mainland, promise of work and hope for the future. Puck is also faced with losing the house and in a move of desperation she enters the Scorpio Races, a race made for the <b>capaill uisce</b>, while Dove is just a regular mare. The odds are against her, the tradition of the islanders are against her, and her gender is against her, let alone that most of the racing horses are going to look upon Dove as a meal, not a competitor. But as scared and worried as she is, Puck is not backing down and her fiery personality jumps off the page, endearing her to the reader with her strength and vulnerability. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"…"“My mother always said that I was born out of a bottle of vinegar instead of born from a womb and that she and my father bathed me in sugar for three days to wash it off. I try to behave, but I always go back to the vinegar.”"…"</i>
</b><br /><br />Sean Kendrick is also a <b>capaill uisce</b> orphan, a witness to the death of his father while participating in one of those Scorpio Races. But just as his father before him, the salt of the sea and the wild beauty of the Water Horses calls to Sean's blood and makes him a part of the ecosystem of the island, addicted to the uncertainty and daily fight for survival. He is only 19 and already has won the race four out of six times. He races on Corr, a Water Horse Stallion, with whom he has a deep bond, a connection deeper than any he has known. He has been trying to bur Corr off of his employer, the rich Horse Yard and stables owner and biggest businessman on the Island. However, the dude keeps Corr over Sean's head as a reason to keep him working for him, since Sean is irreplaceable when it comes to working with the water beasts. He captures them, trains them and rides them, as well as gentles them enough to be ridden by others. He is an expert in a trade known by less than a handful and his boss knows it. But so does the rich dude's son, who is jealous and kindles a deep hatred and need to bring Sean down. However, if he wins the race this year, Sean will get the opportunity to finally buy his beloved Stallion. But that was before he met Puck…<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"…“Does anyone ask you why you stay, Sean Kendrick?"<br />"They do."<br />"And why do you?"<br />"The sky and the sand and the sea and Corr.”"…"</i>
</b><br /><br />In some way the two of them, Sean and Puck, are the heart of the Island. They and those like them keep <br />Thisby alive and its traditions with it. No one knows why the Water Horses have chosen this Island to gather on, no one knows much about them at all. But they show and victimize, as well as personify the image of this otherwise poverty-stricken island… As much as the locals hate the death the <b>capaill uisce</b> leave behind, they are also beholden for their economic existence to them, as well as defining their cultural uniqueness. The attempts of the locals to domesticate those wild beasts are more successful the farther away they are from the shore, since the Sea speaks and calls to them, making them wild with yearning for it, and able to tear all that stands between them and the water apart. However, they would not leave this island, thus not existing anywhere but there… I was mesmerized by their duality of nature!!! <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"…“Tell me what it's like. The race."<br />"What it's like is a battle. A mess of horses and men and blood. The fastest and strongest of what is left from two weeks of preparation on the sand. It's the surf in your face, the deadly magic of November on your skin, the Scorpio drums in the place of your heartbeat. It's speed, if you're lucky. It's life and it's death or it's both, and there's nothing like it.” "…"</i>
</b><br /><br />This story is slow, but so deeply emotional, it is worth every sentence with which it unfolds in front of us. It has Fantastic Water Horses, but it is raw and real as any Stainbeck I have ever read, and just as impactful in its own way. The beauty of both strengths and weaknesses of the human spirit are exposed with the gorgeous prose the author weaves around as a spell. Maggie's goal of the readers feeling like they have their toes in the sand and the chill wind of November pelting the salt of the sea into their skin, is achieved to a maximum and as I finished the story, I felt grief at losing those almost tactile sensations… If I was to ask for anything more, it would be to have more of this world, more about our characters and much, much more of Corr and Dove:):):)<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"…“It's easy to convince men to love you, Puck. All you have to do is be a mountain they have to climb or a poem they don't understand. Something that makes them feel strong or clever. It's why they love the ocean.”"…"</i>
</b><br /><br />I love this quote!!!!!! <br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and may you always find what you need in the pages of a Good Book!!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13164405247347158557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_185244176" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185244176" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185244176?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA Fantasy Fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Arlene by: </span>
      Street Corner Booker Tour - ARC Flannery
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185244176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9456847483570274747"><b>Absolutely fantasical! More please...</b><br/> <br/><i>First off, a huge thanks to Flannery from <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>thereadventurer</a> who is touring this book with the Street Corner Bookers and allowed me to experience this crazy sauce of a book! Thank you!</i><br/> <br/>Wow! Just wow!! Maggie Stiefvater has definitely cemented her status in the YA genre and <b>Scorpio Races</b> is her full access ticket to the game. I've enjoyed her Mercy Falls trilogy for over a couple of years, but this book has definitely pulled her away from the pack and shown she </span>
  <span id="freeText9456847483570274747" style="display:none"><b>Absolutely fantasical! More please...</b><br /> <br /><i>First off, a huge thanks to Flannery from <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com" rel="nofollow noopener">thereadventurer</a> who is touring this book with the Street Corner Bookers and allowed me to experience this crazy sauce of a book! Thank you!</i><br /> <br />Wow! Just wow!! Maggie Stiefvater has definitely cemented her status in the YA genre and <b>Scorpio Races</b> is her full access ticket to the game. I've enjoyed her Mercy Falls trilogy for over a couple of years, but this book has definitely pulled her away from the pack and shown she has what it takes to deliver a novel that will have you falling for the characters, emerging yourself in the setting, and feeling the magic. <br /> <br />If I had to choose one thing that Steifvater excels in, I'd have to say it's her ability to make you feel a part of the setting. She has a way of bringing it to life for the reader, whether it's the cold icy woods of Mercy Falls, or the cliff-side ocean breeze of Skarmouth. She creates such vivid back-drop that you can actually imagine along with the characters having ocean mist spray your face and the sea water confuse your senses. Well done! <br /> <br />This story takes place on the small island of Skarmouth. A place where riders compete in a deadly race every November with capaill uisce (pronounced copple ishka) which are intense and predatory water horses that emerge from the sea. These stallions aren't your normal racing thoroughbreds. These mystical creatures feed on blood and require charms and magic to ride, and at any moment they can turn on their rider and attack. The Scorpio Races is a high stakes game that only the best men enter to compete.<br /> <br />That's until Puck (Kate) Connolly finds herself not only orphaned when her parents fall victim to these savage horses that crave blood, but also when her older brother Gabe decides to abandon her and Finn, the youngest of the three, to the mainland. Kate decides to enter the Scorpio Races to try and stop her brother from leaving and hopefully win the money to make ends meet.<br /> <br />In order for her to win though, she'll have to race against Sean Kendrick, a four time champion in the games. Sean is drawn to the games and the ocean that knows him by name. His moves are influenced by magic as he draws circles in the sand and whispers commands to his beast Corr to control its power. Sean knows what it takes to win the race and his stallion is the one to beat. Winning the game for him, though, isn't about money, but very few know his true motivation.<br /> <br />This story is highly character driven and legend induced. There were so many characters that I fell for especially Sean, who let me tell you is nothing like Sam from Shiver. He's fierce and commanding and probably has never read a line of poetry or plucked a guitar string in his life. ^^ Puck is a worthy main character as well. She's strong and determined and willing to do what it takes for her and Finn to survive. She's rough around the edges and probably can't make her hands clean enough to cook a chicken, but that doesn't stop her from trying to survive the game. I also loved Puck's younger bother Finn. He's ever awkward and extremely loyal to Puck. He's like a fey, you don't thank him or ever give him a compliment. There's just something about him that makes Finn so hug-worthy.<br /> <br />Overall, this book is so much more than racing to the finish line. It's about proving to yourself that you're stronger than others define you to be. It's about pushing yourself to that place that reveals who you really are and what you're truly capable of. Yes, this book mixes in a light romance, but the bond between these two racers is beyond the normal attraction, it's about knowing what you're willing to sacrifice to earn what you really need. Absolutely beautiful!<br /> <br />So if you can't tell by now, I loved this book. <b>Scorpio Races</b> is Triple Crown worthy blending fantasy, magic and romance for a high adventure race to the finish! A must read for fans of Stiefvater and anyone that's looking to experience a magical adventure. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9456847483570274747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_241619791" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241619791" />
    <a title="Tamora Pierce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1451591-tamora-pierce"><img alt="Tamora Pierce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442439344p2/1451591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241619791?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tamora Pierce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tamora Pierce" href="/user/show/1451591-tamora-pierce">Tamora Pierce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1451591-tamora-pierce?shelf=fantasy-ya-yr">fantasy-ya-yr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241619791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13810884805883267833">On a small island in the Scorpio Sea, men and boys strive to capture the deadly, killer water horses that come onto the land from the ocean. If they can master these mounts, they can ride in the yearly races for honor, glory, and big cash bets. Sean Kendrick races for his father, killed by the same water horse he rides now, and for the horse farm he works for as chief hostler. He has won the Scorpio Races four times and understands the water horses like no one else. Puck Connolly, on the other h</span>
  <span id="freeText13810884805883267833" style="display:none">On a small island in the Scorpio Sea, men and boys strive to capture the deadly, killer water horses that come onto the land from the ocean. If they can master these mounts, they can ride in the yearly races for honor, glory, and big cash bets. Sean Kendrick races for his father, killed by the same water horse he rides now, and for the horse farm he works for as chief hostler. He has won the Scorpio Races four times and understands the water horses like no one else. Puck Connolly, on the other hand, has everything against her. She is a girl. She has never ridden a water horse, and plans to ride her own normal horse in the races. And if she doesn't win, she and her younger brother will lose their family farm. <br /><br />Both Puck and Sean are outsiders. Sean is feared by some, treated with awe by others, hated by the son of the man he works for. Puck is despised and scorned--no girl has ever ridden in the races, though they began in honor of a goddess whose rites were observed--are still observed--by a priestess. The reader is constantly reminded that blood and pain are the cost of the games and that Puck and her gentle mount Dove really have no chance at all. But there is something about Puck, her understanding, and her stubborn courage that speaks to the loner Sean, and that might make the difference for both of them and their mounts.<br /><br />Maggie gets better with every book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13810884805883267833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=recommendations">recommendations</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2255768167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11647661102407015782"><a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/11/14/the-scorpio-races/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review</a> ✍️ <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> 📖 <a href='https://twitter.com/Hamad9626' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href='https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> 📷<br/><br/> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“It is the first day of November and so, today, someone will die.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/> <br/>★ It has been a couple of years since I read a novel by Maggie, I love Maggie’s writing and although it felt a bit different from TRC. I am not an expert when it comes to horses, my experience with these creatures is riding on the back of one when I was young and that’s it. This does not mean I did not enjoy it because I did.<br/><br/>★ I shamefully confess that it took me a couple of</span>
  <span id="freeText11647661102407015782" style="display:none"><a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/11/14/the-scorpio-races/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> ✍️ <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> 📖 <a href="https://twitter.com/Hamad9626" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> 📷<br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“It is the first day of November and so, today, someone will die.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /> <br />★ It has been a couple of years since I read a novel by Maggie, I love Maggie’s writing and although it felt a bit different from TRC. I am not an expert when it comes to horses, my experience with these creatures is riding on the back of one when I was young and that’s it. This does not mean I did not enjoy it because I did.<br /><br />★ I shamefully confess that it took me a couple of chapters to realize that Puck is a girl and I thought the Sean and Puck are both boys and we are getting both POVs to see the competition between them! The multiple POV worked well in this book to give us a different look at this world. I think it really empowers women and discusses the discrimination they face in every day life. And it did this without trying so hard and without feeling forced, it was just a natural part of the story.<br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “Boys,’ she says, ‘just aren’t very good at being afraid.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /> <br />★ I would not say the fantasy elements were complex. It was very simple and the story was a mix of everything: fantasy and contemporary and romance, so there is something for fans of all genres in the book. I expected a different thing from the story and more fantasy elements but I felt that was not the point and Maggie in her award speech said that it is not a book about water horses but much more and I exactly felt that. It is a book about family and friends and sacrifice. About hardwork and horses. It is a book about the whole society.<br /><br />★ I think the plot was predictable and I knew what will happen at an early point in the book, especially that there was romance involved in it. But as I said above, it is a book about the journey and not the destination.<br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“There are moments that you’ll remember for the rest of your life and there are moments that you think you’ll remember for the rest of your life, and it’s not often they turn out to be the same moment.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />★ Summary: I am not going to be raving about this book for a long time, I am sure I will forget most of it and remember a few moments after a few months. I am still giving it 4 stars because I did not find anything wrong with it structure wise. It was a well written and edited book.<br /><br />You can get more books from <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=2611996" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_2120358997" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120358997" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120358997?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=unexpectedly-good">unexpectedly-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=emotionally-intense">emotionally-intense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120358997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18211410154999291397"><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races' title='The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Scorpio Races</a> is such a beautifully written tale, I swear I could cry. In retrospect, I did cry while reading the book. In fact, I’ve experienced a dozen different emotions while reading. The entire story was exciting, intriguing, terrifying, hilarious, romantic, inspiring, fantastical and heartwarming. I adored it. <br/><br/>It’s funny because I was never a fan of Ms. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater' title='Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maggie Stiefvater</a>. I tried reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13547386.Shiver' title='Shiver by Karen Robards' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shiver</a> but got so bored I didn’t even finish it. I gave her a second chance in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_' title='The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Raven Boys</a> and even thou</span>
  <span id="freeText18211410154999291397" style="display:none"><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races" title="The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Scorpio Races</a> is such a beautifully written tale, I swear I could cry. In retrospect, I did cry while reading the book. In fact, I’ve experienced a dozen different emotions while reading. The entire story was exciting, intriguing, terrifying, hilarious, romantic, inspiring, fantastical and heartwarming. I adored it. <br /><br />It’s funny because I was never a fan of Ms. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater" title="Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Maggie Stiefvater</a>. I tried reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13547386.Shiver" title="Shiver by Karen Robards" rel="nofollow noopener">Shiver</a> but got so bored I didn’t even finish it. I gave her a second chance in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_" title="The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Raven Boys</a> and even though I liked it enough, I thought it was nothing impressive that I only ended with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17347389.The_Dream_Thieves__The_Raven_Cycle___2_" title="The Dream Thieves (The Raven Cycle, #2) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Dream Thieves</a> and decided not to push through with the series. <br /><br />But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races" title="The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Scorpio Races</a> is a lot different from her other books that after reading the prologue, I was already sure I’d fall in love which is weird because the book is just basically about wild, ugly, devilish horses based on Celtic myth also called <i>capaill uisce</i> pronounced as “copple ooshka” that sprout from the ocean. These creatures can be compared to sharks but the former are a lot worse because they’re both land and sea creatures and could gallop. (omg!) Their grotesque, wicked grin could give you nightmares. Ack! <br /><br />But the plotline is completely amazing. These wild horses and their riders will race every November in what the town calls as the “Scorpio Races”. It’s dangerous and life threatening but <b>Puck</b>, our heroine must (for a lot of important reasons) join the races and take her chances on her ole regular horse called <b> Dove </b>. In joining, Puck defies their culture by being the first girl ever to join the races and tests her odds against all these awesome riders including the four time Scorpio Races champion, <b>Sean Kendrick</b>. *blushes*<br /><br />Afgdkhajklmmnsnbklp! Gaaaaah! It’s just so gorgeously written with a cast of fully developed, unforgettable characters, picturesque setting and adorably subtle romance. I can’t even. Also, Puck is hilarious! <br /><br /><b> “I’m a bit ashamed to recall that I told Brian that if he died and kept me from my cinnamon twist, I’d spit on his grave”</b><br /><br /><b>"I know that his nose is big enough to hide acorns in.”</b><br /><br />Lol! So there! I’m sorry I couldn’t come up with a more coherent review because I couldn’t contain my fangirling. What I’m pretty sure of is that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626594.The_Scorpio_Races" title="The Scorpio Races by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Scorpio Races</a> will make a spot in my top 5 favorites reads of 2017. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="18211410154999291397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3479543950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3479543950" />
    <a title="Lia Carstairs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75966379-lia-carstairs"><img alt="Lia Carstairs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605829031p2/75966379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3479543950?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lia Carstairs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lia Carstairs" href="/user/show/75966379-lia-carstairs">Lia Carstairs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75966379-lia-carstairs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75966379-lia-carstairs?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3479543950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2370853471717598570"><pre>
  <b>"He is slow, and the sea sings to us both, but he returns to me."</b>
</pre><br/>My first <b>Maggie Stiefvater</b> book and I was <b>
  <i>not</i>
</b> disappointed.😭😍<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596827566ra/29931166.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>That last line especially, really got me.🥺❤️ <br/><br/>Never thought I could love the <i>
  <b>capaill uisce</b>
</i> given how <b>bloody monstrous</b> they are—I mean, they <b>do</b> love snacking on humans.😬<br/><br/>Reading about <b>Sean & Corr</b> and <b>Puck & Dove</b> makes me really wish I had that kind of relationship with a horse or better yet <b>
  <i>actually have a horse</i>
</b>.<br/><br/>I've only ridden a horse a few times, but it so</span>
  <span id="freeText2370853471717598570" style="display:none"><pre>
  <b>"He is slow, and the sea sings to us both, but he returns to me."</b>
</pre><br>My first <b>Maggie Stiefvater</b> book and I was <b>
  <i>not</i>
</b> disappointed.😭😍<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596827566ra/29931166.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>That last line especially, really got me.🥺❤️ <br><br>Never thought I could love the <i>
  <b>capaill uisce</b>
</i> given how <b>bloody monstrous</b> they are—I mean, they <b>do</b> love snacking on humans.😬<br><br>Reading about <b>Sean &amp; Corr</b> and <b>Puck &amp; Dove</b> makes me really wish I had that kind of relationship with a horse or better yet <b>
  <i>actually have a horse</i>
</b>.<br><br>I've only ridden a horse a few times, but it sounds so beautiful having such a close friendship with them.🥰<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596828426ra/29932003.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Maggie Stiefvater</b> did such an amazing job describing the world and it's creatures. I could actually picture <b>Thisby</b> so well, and imagine how flying on the <b>water horse</b> was. She has this way of writing that just makes you feel like you're actually experiencing the same things as the characters. (or maybe that's just me😅)<br><br>And I absolutely love <b>Kate (Puck) Connolly</b>. Not only was she the first women to be entering <b>The Scorpio Races</b> but she wasn't even riding a <i>
  <b>capaill uisce</b>
</i> and instead just a regular horse. The other men also racing of course didn't like that she was entering and tried many times, unsuccessfully, to get her to quit. Of course, I loved how Kate fought back and continued to argue with them despite that they were ganging up on her. Such a strong female character! And <b>Sean</b> spoke up for her too!!! Those two. They're the perfect pair.🥺🥰 <br><br><pre>
  <b>"This island runs on courage, not blood," he says.</b>
</pre><br>I love you <b>Sean Kendrick</b>.💖<br><br>Also, I didn't even know water horse were mythological creatures! I only just learned from searching up <i>
  <b>capaill uisce</b>
</i> on Google. And that's <b>after</b> I finished the book.<br><br>Talk about an <b>epic fail</b>.🤦‍♀️<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596835461i/29932310._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><s>Matthew</s> <b>Mutt</b> Malvern was such a despicable character. I was so happy with what he got at the end of the novel. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>DEATH😈</b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He was way too cruel to both the horses and Sean. <b>Especially Sean.</b>😥 <b>BAD MUTT👿</b><br><br>Although his father, <b>Benjamin Malvern</b> was also a jerk for not wanting to sell Corr to Sean <i>knowing</i> that nobody else would be able to tame him like Sean could. I could tell though that he held Sean in high regard, with what he said to <s>Matthew</s> <b>Mutt</b>😜. <br><br><i>
  <b>“So he’s practically a son,” Holly says. “That explains the bond. These horses all bear his handprint, don’t they? Seems to me he’s the logical heir to the Malvern Yard, if you were asking me.”<br><br>Benjamin Malvern had been looking at his son, who was staring back at him, but when Holly finishes, Malvern’s eyes sweep over me in my suit and he purses his lips. “In many ways, Mr. Holly, I think that is very true.” He looks back up to Mutt and adds, “In most ways.”</b>
</i><br><br><s>Maybe I feel a little bad for <b>Mutt</b> seeing that his own father doesn't think much of him.</s> Nope never mind. He doesn't deserve my pity.😒<br><br>Oooo that reminds me! I was suspicious of <b>George Holly</b> at first, but actually, he's an amazing guy! He was such a nice and clever man to both Sean and Kate. <b>Holly</b> was an American visiting <b>Thisby</b> to check out the offers he could buy. <br><br>You see, usually I find the men in those business suits to be the suspicious and secretly plotting something evil. xD well there was definitely nothing wrong with him and he clearly wanted to help out Sean with his dreams. <b>What a cool American.</b>👌😎<br><br>Oh and I just adored <b>Finn!</b> He was definitely a much better brother than Gabe -&gt; who I really hated in the beginning of the novel, although now I can understand him more and why he wanted to leave <b>Thisby</b> to go to the mainland. Still, <b>Finn</b> was a super supportive little brother.🥺 The conversations between Kate and Finn were funny too.😂<br><br><i>
  <b>“You made this?"<br>Finn looks at me. "No, Saint Anthony brought it to me in the night. He was very put out I didn't give it to you right then.”</b>
</i><br><br>xD and Kate is a master with her retorts. I could never compare.🤣<br><br><i>
  <b>I hear laughter and someone asks if I need help, not in a nice way. I snarl, "What I need is for your mother to have thought a little harder nine months before your birthday."</b>
</i><br><br>I shall never forget Kate, Sean, the <i>
  <b>capaill uisce</b>
</i>, and <b>especially</b> this scene:<br><pre>
  <b>"I will not be your weakness, Sean Kendrick."<br>He says, very softly, 'It's late for that, Puck."</b>
</pre><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596837669ra/29932363.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://chainofnovels.wordpress.com/2020/08/07/the-scorpio-races-by-maggie-stiefvater-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">|Blog|</a>
</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2370853471717598570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('I6ylRuWxuUOwNOJj4iN8gtY8t78NIgBgg36T3Hc6MEoZisyUXu9wKxcfVgIV1nZdAGNQd8OvjgfYANVtunnC0A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KHz27zR5sjIL/MUodxheG8KM/dTaPTvEsXmUlHMEWogSWp89jyd7WqzXcUmA7VTEFNMaHBSwtaPqB9IlvkeoEg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer11938277329818062394">New York Times bestselling author of The Shiver Trilogy, The Raven Cycle, and The Scorpio Races. Artist. Driver of things with wheels. Avid reader.<br/><br/>All of Maggie Stiefvater's life decisions have been formed by a desire to leave a mark, resulting in spray-painted cars, sharpie-covered computer printers, ink-splattered walls, and stories told in books, in magazines, and on stages. Maggie Stiefvater l</span>
  <span id="freeText11938277329818062394" style="display:none">New York Times bestselling author of The Shiver Trilogy, The Raven Cycle, and The Scorpio Races. Artist. Driver of things with wheels. Avid reader.<br /><br />All of Maggie Stiefvater's life decisions have been formed by a desire to leave a mark, resulting in spray-painted cars, sharpie-covered computer printers, ink-splattered walls, and stories told in books, in magazines, and on stages. Maggie Stiefvater lives in the middle of nowhere, Virginia with her charmingly straight-laced husband, two kids, two neurotic dogs, and a 1973 Camaro named Loki.<br /><br /></span>
